Only one queue sort\\n463: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\\n464: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\\n465: \\tPlugin\\n466: \\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\\n467: \\tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\\n468: }\\n469: \\n470: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\\n471: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\\n472: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\\n473: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\\n474: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\\n475: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\\n476: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\\n477: // and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\\n478: //\\n479: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\\n480: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\\n481: // And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\\n482: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\\n483: \\tPlugin\\n484: \\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\\n485: \\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\\n486: \\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n487: \\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\n488: \\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\n489: \\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\\n490: \\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\\n491: \\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\\n492: \\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\\n493: \\t//\\n494: \\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\n495: \\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\\n496: }\\n497: \\n498: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\n499: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\n500: // state.\\n501: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\n502: \\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n503: \\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n504: \\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n505: \\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n506: \\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n507: \\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n508: }\\n509: \\n510: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreFilter\\\" plugins.\\n511: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\\n512: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\\n513: \\tPlugin\\n514: \\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\\n515: \\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\\n516: \\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\\n517: \\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\\n518: \\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\".\\n519: \\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\\n520: \\t//\\n521: \\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\\n522: \\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n523: \\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n524: \\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\\n525: \\t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\\n526: \\t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\\n527: \\t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\\n528: \\t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\\n529: \\t// Filter again on a specific node.\\n530: \\tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\\n531: }\\n532: \\n533: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\\n534: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\\n535: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\\n536: // These plugins should return \\\"Success\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\" in Status.code.\\n537: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\\n538: // Anything other than \\\"Success\\\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\\n539: // running the pod.\\n540: type FilterPlugin interface {\\n541: \\tPlugin\\n542: \\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\\n543: \\t// All FilterPlugins should return \\\"Success\\\" to declare that\\n544: \\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n545: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n546: \\t//\\n547: \\t// \\\"Error\\\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\\n548: \\t//\\n549: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n550: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n551: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n552: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n553: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n554: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n555: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n556: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n557: }\\n558: \\n559: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. These plugins are called\\n560: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\\n561: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\\n562: \\tPlugin\\n563: \\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\\n564: \\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n565: \\t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\\n566: \\t//\\n567: \\t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\\n568: \\t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n569: \\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n570: \\t//\\n571: \\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\\n572: \\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\\n573: \\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\\n574: \\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\\n575: \\t//\\n576: \\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\\n577: \\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\\n578: \\t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\\n579: \\t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\\n580: \\tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusReader) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\\n581: }\\n582: \\n583: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \\\"PreScore\\\" plugin. PreScore is an\\n584: // informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\\n585: // that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\\n586: // state or to generate logs/metrics.\\n587: type PreScorePlugin interface {\\n588: \\tPlugin\\n589: \\t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\\n590: \\t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\\n591: \\t// the pod will be rejected\\n592: \\t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\\n593: \\t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n594: \\tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\\n595: }\\n596: \\n597: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\\n598: type ScoreExtensions interface {\\n599: \\t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \\\"Score\\\"\\n600: \\t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\\n601: \\t// a success status.\\n602: \\tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\\n603: }\\n604: \\n605: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Score\\\" plugins to rank\\n606: // nodes that passed the filtering phase.\\n607: type ScorePlugin interface {\\n608: \\tPlugin\\n609: \\t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\\n610: \\t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\\n611: \\t// the pod will be rejected.\\n612: \\tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\\n613: \\n614: \\t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\\n615: \\tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\\n616: }\\n617: \\n618: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\\n619: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\\n620: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\\n621: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\\n622: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\\n623: // rejection of the pod.\\n624: type ReservePlugin interface {\\n625: \\tPlugin\\n626: \\t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\\n627: \\t// updated. These plugins are called at the\n534: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n535: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n536: // These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n537: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n538: // Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n539: // running the pod.\n540: type FilterPlugin interface {\n541: \tPlugin\n542: \t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n543: \t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n544: \t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n545: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n546: \t//\n547: \t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n548: \t//\n549: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n550: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n551: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n552: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n553: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n554: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n555: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n556: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n557: }\n558: \n559: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n560: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n561: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n562: \tPlugin\n563: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n564: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n565: \t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n566: \t//\n567: \t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n568: \t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n569: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n570: \t//\n571: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n572: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n573: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n574: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n575: \t//\n576: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n577: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n578: \t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n579: \t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n580: \tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusReader) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n581: }\n582: \n583: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. PreScore is an\n584: // informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\n585: // that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n586: // state or to generate logs/metrics.\n587: type PreScorePlugin interface {\n588: \tPlugin\n589: \t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n590: \t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n591: \t// the pod will be rejected\n592: \t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n593: \t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n594: \tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\n595: }\n596: \n597: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\n598: type ScoreExtensions interface {\n599: \t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n600: \t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n601: \t// a success status.\n602: \tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n603: }\n604: \n605: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n606: // nodes that passed the filtering phase.\n607: type ScorePlugin interface {\n608: \tPlugin\n609: \t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\n610: \t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\n611: \t// the pod will be rejected.\n612: \tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\n613: \n614: \t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\n615: \tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\n616: }\n617: \n618: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\n619: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\n620: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\n621: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n622: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n623: // rejection of the pod.\n624: type ReservePlugin interface {\n625: \tPlugin\n626: \t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n627: \t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\n628: \t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\n629: \tReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n630: \t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\n631: \t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\n632: \t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\n633: \t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\n634: \t// method for the same plugin was not called.\n635: \tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n636: }\n637: \n638: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreBind\" plugins.\n639: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\n640: type PreBindPlugin interface {\n641: \tPlugin\n642: \t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\n643: \t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\n644: \tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n645: }\n646: \n647: // PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PostBind\" plugins.\n648: // These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\n649: type PostBindPlugin interface {\n650: \tPlugin\n651: \t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\n652: \t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\n653: \t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\n654: \t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\n655: \tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n656: }\n657: \n658: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Permit\" plugins.\n659: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\n660: type PermitPlugin interface {\n661: \tPlugin\n662: \t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\n663: \t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n664: \t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n665: \t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n666: \t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \"wait\", the framework will wait only\n667: \t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\n668: \tPermit(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\n669: }\n670: \n671: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Bind\" plugins. Bind\n672: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\n673: type BindPlugin interface {\n674: \tPlugin\n675: \t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\n676: \t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n677: \t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\n678: \t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\n679: \t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\n680: \t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\n681: \tBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n682: }\n683: \n684: // Framework manages the set of plugins in use by the scheduling framework.\n685: // Configured plugins are called at specified points in a scheduling context.\n686: type Framework interface {\n687: \tHandle\n688: \n689: \t// PreEnqueuePlugins returns the registered preEnqueue plugins.\n690: \tPreEnqueuePlugins() []PreEnqueuePlugin\n691: \n692: \t// EnqueueExtensions returns the registered Enqueue extensions.\n693: \tEnqueueExtensions() []EnqueueExtensions\n694: \n695: \t// QueueSortFunc returns the function to sort pods in scheduling queue\n696: \tQueueSortFunc() LessFunc\n697: \n698: \t// RunPreFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PreFilter plugins. It returns\n699: \t// *Status and its code is set to non-success if any of the plugins returns\n700: \t// anything but Success. If a non-success status is returned, then the scheduling\n701: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes@cc415b71c5f2cc8ea30f2574c7124b06a9f1b78c/-/blob/pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go%3FL430-700"}}}
